And the Imam may grant nafal by his statement: 'Whoever kills a slain person, he gets his weapon (salab),' and by his statement to the detachment: 'I have made for you one quarter' meaning it is recommended for him at the time of fighting to urge and encourage. Or 'Whoever takes something, it is for him' after the khums. And he may give nafal after the spoils are brought to safety from the khums. The spoils (ghanimah) and its plural, and it is four hundred men for example. And the Imam may grant nafal etc. It is said: 'nafala' with tashdid or takhfif, both are eloquent. Nafal (with two fathas) plural anfal. The condition for the permissibility of nafal is that it be before the spoils are brought to safety in the land of Islam. Nafal is giving something extra over the shares of the participants. It is recommended for the Imam to promise a fighter an additional amount over his share by saying: 'Whoever kills a slain person, he gets his salab.' The person killed is called 'qatil' considering what he will become, as in the verse: 'I see myself pressing wine' (Yusuf:36). And al-salab (with two fathas, the lam may be sakina) means the booty taken, plural aslab. In technical terms, it is what the killer takes from his opponent of weapons and clothes, as the author will mention. And by his saying to the detachment: 'I have made for you one quarter, or half, or one third' after the khums, because it is an incitement to fight, and it is recommended. Allah said: 'O Prophet, urge the believers to fight' (al-Anfal:65). He urged through nafal for fighting, saying: 'Whoever kills a slain person and has proof of it, he gets his weapon (salab),' narrated by Ahmad, Bukhari, and Muslim. The Messenger of Allah gave one quarter after the khums on his return, narrated by Ahmad and Abu Dawud. He used to give one quarter at the beginning and one third on the return, narrated by Ahmad, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. His statement 'after the khums' is not a condition apparently, because if he gave nafal of one quarter of the total, it is permissible, it just happened that way. Don't you see that if he gave the entire spoils to a detachment, it is permissible, so this is even more suitable. It does not fall under the generality. And nafal may be other than what is mentioned here, like dirhams and dinars. Or he says: 'Whoever takes something, it is for him.' The Imam includes himself among those who kill a slain person and get his salab, so if he himself kills a man after saying that, according to qiyas he does not deserve the salab because the speaker's word (against himself), but according to istihsan he does deserve it because it is not a matter of judgment, but a matter of entitlement to spoils. For this reason, everyone who is entitled to a share or a small portion of booty is included, and there is no accusation against him. Contrary to if he says: 'Whoever I kill, his salab is for me,' where he does not deserve it because he singled himself out, making him suspect. And contrary to if he says: 'Whoever among you kills a slain person, he gets his salab,' where he is not included because he distinguished himself. And he only deserves the salab by killing if the killed person is permissible to kill. Thus he does not deserve the salab for killing women, children, and insane persons. He does deserve it for killing a patient, a hired laborer among them, a trader in their army, and a dhimmi who broke the treaty and came out to them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/427) (Fath) 'And by his statement' meaning it is permissible for him to give nafal by his statement. (Ayni) 'After the khums' meaning after taking the khums, and it is not a restriction because he may give the entire spoils to a detachment. (T) 'And he gives nafal after the spoils are brought to safety' etc. It is restricted by 'after bringing to safety' because before bringing to safety, it is permissible to give nafal from the whole or from four-fifths. After bringing to safety, he may not give nafal from the four-fifths because the right of the participants is confirmed by bringing to safety in the abode, and they have no right in the khums, so it is permissible to give nafal from it. It may not be said that this voids the right of the three categories; that is also not allowed. For we say: the payment -
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage discusses the rules of nafal (extra grants) given by the Imam to soldiers to encourage bravery in battle. The Imam may announce, 'Whoever kills an enemy, may take his weapon and clothes (salab)' or 'To this detachment I give one quarter (of the spoils) after deducting the khums.' Nafal is recommended (mandub) before the spoils are brought to safety (ihraz). The author cites hadith evidence from the Prophet's practice. He clarifies that the phrase 'after the khums' is not a strict condition; the Imam could give from the entire spoils if he wishes. The Imam includes himself in the offer; according to qiyas he would not deserve the salab, but istihsan gives it to him because it is not a judicial matter but a right to spoils. The salab is only given if the killed person was a legitimate target (not women, children, or insane). Those who are legitimate targets include patients, hired fighters, traders in the enemy camp, and dhimmis who broke their covenant.

Key Terms
نفل (nafal): An extra grant given by the Imam to soldiers beyond their regular share of spoils.
سلب (salab): The weapons and clothes of a slain enemy taken by the killer.
إحراز (ihraz): Bringing the spoils to safety in the land of Islam, after which the rights of participants are fixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, by qiyas

D) No, because it would be unfair to others

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the Imam to grant nafal before ihraz and, by istihsan, to include himself in the reward, overriding the qiyas principle.

The Imam's Authority to Grant Tanfil in Jihad
Permissibility and method of tanfil from spoils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tanfil, identify its condition (before ihtiyaz), and apply the hadith proof to determine when the imam can grant extra spoils.

Core Idea
Tanfil is a recommended incentive from the imam before booty is secured; after that, it is limited to the khums.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the concept of tanfil – giving extra spoils to fighters as encouragement. The imam has the authority to grant such incentives, but the timing and source are crucial. Let's explore the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tanfil is the act of the imam giving something extra to fighters beyond their regular share. According to the Hanafi school, it is mustahabb (recommended) for the imam, not obligatory.
The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) due to the Prophet's practice.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The text states that tanfil from the general spoils (the four-fifths) is permissible only before the booty is secured in Dar al-Islam (ihtiyaz). After that, it is only allowed from the khums (the fifth reserved for Allah, the Prophet, etc.).
This condition protects the fighters' confirmed rights in the four-fifths after securing.
3
State the methods of tanfil
The imam may use two explicit methods: (1) saying 'Whoever kills an enemy, his salb (spoils of the slain) is his,' or (2) telling a detachment 'I have given you a quarter/half/third after the khums.' He may also say 'Whoever takes something, it is his,' but only within the khums after ihtiyaz.
The second method is recommended during battle as encouragement.
4
Examine the primary evidence (dalil)
The hadith: 'Whoever kills an enemy and has proof, his spoils are his' (sahih). The Prophet also practiced tanfil by giving a quarter after the khums on return from battle and a third on the initial sortie. The Quranic verse (8:65) commands encouragement, which includes tanfil.
The dalil is ahad but supports the sunnah ruling.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and its practical effect
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools do not permit tanfil from the khums after the booty is secured, whereas the Hanafi school allows it. This difference affects how a commander may promise extra rewards after the battle.
The Hanafi position is based on istihsan, considering the khums is not yet allocated to specific recipients until the imam distributes it.

Source Text

وبأن يقول للسرية: جعلت لكم الربع أو النصف أو الثلث بعد الخمس؛ لأنه تحريض على القتال، وهو مندوب إليه، قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ حَرّضِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عَلَى الْقِتَالِ (الأنفال: ٦٥)، وحرض عليه بالتنفيل على القتال، فقال: "من قتل قتيلاً له عليه بينة فله سلبه"، رواه أحمد والبخاري ومسلم ونفل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الربع بعد الخمس في رجعته رواه أحمد وأبو داود، وكان ينفل عليه في البداية الربع، وفي الرجعة الثلث، رواه أحمد والترمذي وابن ماجه، وقوله: "بعد الخمس" ليس على سبيل الشرط ظاهراً؛ لأنه لو نفل بربع الكل، جاز، وإنما وقع ذلك اتفاقاً، ألا ترى أنه لو نفل للسرية بالكل، جاز، فهذا أولى.

Book of Military Expeditions and Jihad. Manner of Division. And the Imam may give extra incentive by his saying: 'Whoever kills an enemy, his spoils are his,' and by his saying to the detachment: 'I have given you a quarter' - i.e., it is recommended for him at the time of fighting as encouragement and motivation - or 'Whoever takes something, it is his' after the khums. And he may give extra incentive after securing (the booty) from the khums. ... [continues]
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the imam's authority to grant tanfil (additional incentive) to the fighters. The author begins by explaining the linguistic meaning of nafal, then states the condition that tanfil is permissible only before the booty is secured in Dar al-Islam. The preferred method is for the imam to say 'Whoever kills an enemy, his salb is his' or to grant a portion of the khums to a detachment. The evidence is from the Prophet's practice and Quranic encouragement. The imam may also include himself in his statement, but if he says 'my salb' he becomes suspect. The salb is only due if the slain person was lawful to kill (e.g., not women, children, or insane). The passage ends by discussing the restriction of tanfil to khums after the booty is secured, because the fighters' rights are confirmed in the four-fifths.

Key Terms
تنفيل (tanfil): Giving something extra to fighters beyond their regular share as an incentive during jihad.
سلب (salb): The spoils taken from a slain enemy combatant: weapons, clothing, mount and its gear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only before securing booty in Dar al-Islam
C) Only after securing booty
D) Only after the battle ends

Key Takeaway
Tanfil is a recommended incentive from the imam before booty is secured; after that, it is limited to the khums.
